# IMPORTANT: Source Code Access

**Local source files are not present.** Your workspace does not contain source code. You **MUST** use Sourcegraph MCP tools to discover, read, and understand code before making any changes.

Use `sg_list_repos` to discover available repositories before searching.


## Required Workflow

1. **Search first** — Use MCP tools to find relevant files and understand existing patterns
2. **Read remotely** — Use `sg_read_file` to read full file contents from Sourcegraph
3. **Edit locally** — Use Edit, Write, and Bash to create or modify files in your working directory
4. **Verify locally** — Run tests with Bash to check your changes

## Tool Selection

| Goal | Tool |
|------|------|
| Exact symbol/string | `sg_keyword_search` |
| Concepts/semantic search | `sg_nls_search` |
| Trace usage/callers | `sg_find_references` |
| See implementation | `sg_go_to_definition` |
| Read full file | `sg_read_file` |
| Browse structure | `sg_list_files` |
| Find repos | `sg_list_repos` |
| Search commits | `sg_commit_search` |
| Track changes | `sg_diff_search` |
| Compare versions | `sg_compare_revisions` |

**Decision logic:**
1. Know the exact symbol? → `sg_keyword_search`
2. Know the concept, not the name? → `sg_nls_search`
3. Need definition of a symbol? → `sg_go_to_definition`
4. Need all callers/references? → `sg_find_references`
5. Need full file content? → `sg_read_file`

## Scoping (Always Do This)

```
repo:^github.com/ORG/REPO$           # Exact repo (preferred)
repo:github.com/ORG/                 # All repos in org
file:.*\.ts$                         # TypeScript only
file:src/api/                        # Specific directory
```

Start narrow. Expand only if results are empty.

## Efficiency Rules

- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than one at a time
- Don't read 20+ remote files without writing code — once you understand the pattern, start implementing

## If Stuck

If MCP search returns no results:
1. Broaden the search query (synonyms, partial identifiers)
2. Try `sg_nls_search` for semantic matching
3. Use `sg_list_files` to browse the directory structure
4. Use `sg_list_repos` to verify the repository name

## Summary

I've identified and documented **13 key files** and **34+ important symbols** that comprise the SharedInformer factory implementation in client-go v0.32.0. Here's what was found:

### Core Components:

1. **Factory Registration** (`informers/factory.go`):
   - `SharedInformerFactory` interface and implementation
   - `NewSharedInformerFactory()` - creates factory instances
   - `Start()`, `Shutdown()`, `WaitForCacheSync()` methods

2. **List-Watch Mechanism** (`tools/cache/listwatch.go`):
   - `ListerWatcher` interface combining List and Watch operations
   - `ListWatch` implementation for API calls
   - `NewListWatchFromClient()` factory function

3. **Reflector Pattern** (`tools/cache/reflector.go`):
   - `Reflector` struct that watches API server and syncs changes
   - `ListAndWatch()` method implementing the core watch loop
   - Resource version tracking and pagination support

4. **Cache Stores** (`tools/cache/store.go`, `index.go`, `thread_safe_store.go`):
   - `Store` interface for basic cache operations
   - `Indexer` interface for efficient lookups
   - `ThreadSafeStore` for concurrent-safe access

5. **DeltaFIFO Queue** (`tools/cache/delta_fifo.go`):
   - Queue connecting Reflector to event handlers
   - Tracks deltas (Added, Updated, Deleted) of objects

6. **SharedInformer** (`tools/cache/shared_informer.go`):
   - `SharedIndexInformer` implementation with event distribution
   - `sharedProcessor` for multi-listener event delivery
   - Integration with cache and controller

7. **Synchronization Tracking** (`tools/cache/synctrack/`):
   - `AsyncTracker` and `Lazy` for sync state tracking

Architecture in client-go v0.32.0\\n\\nThe SharedInformer factory is the core mechanism in Kubernetes client-go for maintaining an eventually-consistent local cache of API server resources. The implementation spans multiple key components:\\n\\n### Factory Registration (informers/factory.go)\\nThe `SharedInformerFactory` interface and `sharedInformerFactory` implementation in `informers/factory.go` provides the main entry point. Functions like `NewSharedInformerFactory()` and `NewSharedInformerFactoryWithOptions()` create factory instances. The factory manages:\\n- A map of informers indexed by object type\\n- Tracking of started vs unstarted informers\\n- Resync period configuration (global and per-type)\\n- Namespace filtering and list option tweaking\\n- Shutdown coordination via WaitGroup\\n\\nKey methods:\\n- `Start()` initializes all registered informers in separate goroutines\\n- `Shutdown()` stops all informers and waits for cleanup\\n- `WaitForCacheSync()` waits for cache synchronization to complete\\n- `InformerFor()` gets or creates a SharedIndexInformer for a given object\\n\\n### Informer Registration (informers/internalinterfaces/factory_interfaces.go)\\nThe internal `SharedInformerFactory` interface defines the minimal contract needed to avoid import cycles. The `NewInformerFunc` type is a function pointer that creates SharedIndexInformers, allowing the factory to instantiate informers for different resource types.\\n\\n### List-Watch Mechanism (tools/cache/listwatch.go)\\nThe `ListerWatcher` interface combines:\\n- `List()` method to fetch all objects matching criteria\\n- `Watch()` method to receive incremental updates\\n\\nThe `ListWatch` implementation provides a concrete instance that wraps REST client calls. `NewListWatchFromClient()` creates ListWatch instances for specific resources, handling field selector configuration and options modification.\\n\\n### Reflector Pattern (tools/cache/reflector.go)\\nThe `Reflector` watches a resource via ListerWatcher and syncs all changes to a Store. Key features:\\n- Handles List/Watch semantics with exponential backoff for failures\\n- Manages resource version tracking for resumable watches\\n- Supports pagination with `WatchListPageSize` for large datasets\\n- Implements optional watchlist streaming mode (UseWatchList)\\n- Customizable error handling via WatchErrorHandler\\n- Resync period support for reconciliation\\n\\nThe Reflector is created by the Controller and drives continuous synchronization with the API server.\\n\\n### Cache Store Implementations (tools/cache/store.go, tools/cache/index.go)\\nThe `Store` interface defines basic cache operations (Add, Update, Delete, Get, List, Replace). The `Indexer` extends Store with indexing capabilities for efficient lookups by field values.\\n\\n`NewStore()` creates a basic unindexed store using `ThreadSafeStore` as the backend.\\n`NewIndexer()` creates an indexed store with configurable index functions.\\n\\n### Thread-Safe Storage (tools/cache/thread_safe_store.go)\\nThe `ThreadSafeStore` interface provides concurrent-safe access to cached objects. Implementation uses:\\n- Mutex-protected access to object maps\\n- Index structures for efficient field-based queries (NamespaceIndex, etc.)\\n- Support for adding indexers dynamically\\n\\n### DeltaFIFO Queue (tools/cache/delta_fifo.go)\\nThe `DeltaFIFO` is a producer-consumer queue that:\\n- Stores objects as Deltas (sequence of operations: Added, Updated, Deleted, Replaced, Sync)\\n- Acts as the intermediary between Reflector (producer) and event handlers (consumers)\\n- Tracks known objects to detect state changes\\n- Supports deduplication and ordering guarantees\\n\\n`NewDeltaFIFOWithOptions()` creates instances with configurable key function and known object tracking.\\n\\n### Controller Orchestration (tools/cache/controller.go)\\nThe `Controller` interface orchestrates the Reflector and DeltaFIFO queue:\\n- Created via `New()` with a Config specifying the queue, ListerWatcher, and ProcessFunc\\n- `Run()` method starts the Reflector in a goroutine and processes queue items\\n- Handles both initial sync and incremental updates\\n\\n### SharedInformer Event Distribution (tools/cache/shared_informer.go)\\nThe `SharedIndexInformer` implementation:\\n- Wraps a Controller and Indexer (the cache)\\n- Uses `sharedProcessor` to distribute cache events to multiple listeners\\n- Each listener is wrapped in a `processorListener` with its own event channel\\n- Supports AddEventHandler() to register ResourceEventHandlers\\n- Provides HasSynced() to check if initial sync is complete\\n- Uses synctrack.Lazy for lazy evaluation of sync state\\n\\n`NewSharedIndexInformer()` creates instances with optional indexers for performance.\\n\\n### Synchronization Tracking (tools/cache/synctrack/)\\nThe synctrack package provides utilities for tracking sync state across multiple goroutines:\\n- `AsyncTracker` helps propagate HasSynced in multi-threaded scenarios\\n- `Lazy` provides lazy evaluation with single computation\\n- `SingleFileTracker` tracks sync state for individual listeners\\n\\n### Complete Flow\\n1. User calls `NewSharedInformerFactory()` to create a factory\\n2. User calls `factory.Start(stopChan)` to initialize all registered informers\\n3. Factory creates informers via `InformerFor()` using NewInformerFuncs\\n4. Each informer creates a SharedIndexInformer with cache (Indexer) and controller\\n5. Controller creates a Reflector with ListerWatcher and DeltaFIFO queue\\n6. Reflector starts `ListAndWatch()` which:\\n   - Calls ListerWatcher.List() to fetch initial objects\\n   - Stores all objects in the DeltaFIFO with Replaced deltas\\n   - Calls ListerWatcher.Watch() to receive incremental updates\\n   - Adds updates to DeltaFIFO as Added/Updated/Deleted deltas\\n7. Controller.Run() processes items from DeltaFIFO:\\n   - Pops Deltas and applies them to the Indexer (cache)\\n   - Invokes registered event handlers\\n8. SharedProcessor distributes events to multiple listeners\\n9. Clients query cache via Indexer.Get() or Lister interfaces\\n10. User calls `factory.Shutdown()` to cleanly stop all informers\\n\\nThis architecture provides an eventually-consistent, efficient, and scalable mechanism for keeping local caches in sync with Kubernetes API server state.\"\n}\n",

The implementation spans multiple key components:\\n\\n### Factory Registration (informers/factory.go)\\nThe `SharedInformerFactory` interface and `sharedInformerFactory` implementation in `informers/factory.go` provides the main entry point. Functions like `NewSharedInformerFactory()` and `NewSharedInformerFactoryWithOptions()` create factory instances. The factory manages:\\n- A map of informers indexed by object type\\n- Tracking of started vs unstarted informers\\n- Resync period configuration (global and per-type)\\n- Namespace filtering and list option tweaking\\n- Shutdown coordination via WaitGroup\\n\\nKey methods:\\n- `Start()` initializes all registered informers in separate goroutines\\n- `Shutdown()` stops all informers and waits for cleanup\\n- `WaitForCacheSync()` waits for cache synchronization to complete\\n- `InformerFor()` gets or creates a SharedIndexInformer for a given object\\n\\n### Informer Registration (informers/internalinterfaces/factory_interfaces.go)\\nThe internal `SharedInformerFactory` interface defines the minimal contract needed to avoid import cycles. The `NewInformerFunc` type is a function pointer that creates SharedIndexInformers, allowing the factory to instantiate informers for different resource types.\\n\\n### List-Watch Mechanism (tools/cache/listwatch.go)\\nThe `ListerWatcher` interface combines:\\n- `List()` method to fetch all objects matching criteria\\n- `Watch()` method to receive incremental updates\\n\\nThe `ListWatch` implementation provides a concrete instance that wraps REST client calls. `NewListWatchFromClient()` creates ListWatch instances for specific resources, handling field selector configuration and options modification.\\n\\n### Reflector Pattern (tools/cache/reflector.go)\\nThe `Reflector` watches a resource via ListerWatcher and syncs all changes to a Store. Key features:\\n- Handles List/Watch semantics with exponential backoff for failures\\n- Manages resource version tracking for resumable watches\\n- Supports pagination with `WatchListPageSize` for large datasets\\n- Implements optional watchlist streaming mode (UseWatchList)\\n- Customizable error handling via WatchErrorHandler\\n- Resync period support for reconciliation\\n\\nThe Reflector is created by the Controller and drives continuous synchronization with the API server.\\n\\n### Cache Store Implementations (tools/cache/store.go, tools/cache/index.go)\\nThe `Store` interface defines basic cache operations (Add, Update, Delete, Get, List, Replace). The `Indexer` extends Store with indexing capabilities for efficient lookups by field values.\\n\\n`NewStore()` creates a basic unindexed store using `ThreadSafeStore` as the backend.\\n`NewIndexer()` creates an indexed store with configurable index functions.\\n\\n### Thread-Safe Storage (tools/cache/thread_safe_store.go)\\nThe `ThreadSafeStore` interface provides concurrent-safe access to cached objects. Implementation uses:\\n- Mutex-protected access to object maps\\n- Index structures for efficient field-based queries (NamespaceIndex, etc.)\\n- Support for adding indexers dynamically\\n\\n### DeltaFIFO Queue (tools/cache/delta_fifo.go)\\nThe `DeltaFIFO` is a producer-consumer queue that:\\n- Stores objects as Deltas (sequence of operations: Added, Updated, Deleted, Replaced, Sync)\\n- Acts as the intermediary between Reflector (producer) and event handlers (consumers)\\n- Tracks known objects to detect state changes\\n- Supports deduplication and ordering guarantees\\n\\n`NewDeltaFIFOWithOptions()` creates instances with configurable key function and known object tracking.\\n\\n### Controller Orchestration (tools/cache/controller.go)\\nThe `Controller` interface orchestrates the Reflector and DeltaFIFO queue:\\n- Created via `New()` with a Config specifying the queue, ListerWatcher, and ProcessFunc\\n- `Run()` method starts the Reflector in a goroutine and processes queue items\\n- Handles both initial sync and incremental updates\\n\\n### SharedInformer Event Distribution (tools/cache/shared_informer.go)\\nThe `SharedIndexInformer` implementation:\\n- Wraps a Controller and Indexer (the cache)\\n- Uses `sharedProcessor` to distribute cache events to multiple listeners\\n- Each listener is wrapped in a `processorListener` with its own event channel\\n- Supports AddEventHandler() to register ResourceEventHandlers\\n- Provides HasSynced() to check if initial sync is complete\\n- Uses synctrack.Lazy for lazy evaluation of sync state\\n\\n`NewSharedIndexInformer()` creates instances with optional indexers for performance.\\n\\n### Synchronization Tracking (tools/cache/synctrack/)\\nThe synctrack package provides utilities for tracking sync state across multiple goroutines:\\n- `AsyncTracker` helps propagate HasSynced in multi-threaded scenarios\\n- `Lazy` provides lazy evaluation with single computation\\n- `SingleFileTracker` tracks sync state for individual listeners\\n\\n### Complete Flow\\n1. User calls `NewSharedInformerFactory()` to create a factory\\n2. User calls `factory.Start(stopChan)` to initialize all registered informers\\n3. Factory creates informers via `InformerFor()` using NewInformerFuncs\\n4. Each informer creates a SharedIndexInformer with cache (Indexer) and controller\\n5. Controller creates a Reflector with ListerWatcher and DeltaFIFO queue\\n6. Reflector starts `ListAndWatch()` which:\\n   - Calls ListerWatcher.List() to fetch initial objects\\n   - Stores all objects in the DeltaFIFO with Replaced deltas\\n   - Calls ListerWatcher.Watch() to receive incremental updates\\n   - Adds updates to DeltaFIFO as Added/Updated/Deleted deltas\\n7. Controller.Run() processes items from DeltaFIFO:\\n   - Pops Deltas and applies them to the Indexer (cache)\\n   - Invokes registered event handlers\\n8. SharedProcessor distributes events to multiple listeners\\n9. Clients query cache via Indexer.Get() or Lister interfaces\\n10. User calls `factory.Shutdown()` to cleanly stop all informers\\n\\nThis architecture provides an eventually-consistent, efficient, and scalable mechanism for keeping local caches in sync with Kubernetes API server state.\"\n}\n",
